The above-listed general expenditure and emergency military expenses include all of the Japanese government's financial system for 1940-41, while deducting several types of special expenditure that are self-liquidating. The total national expenditure for 1940-41 is 9,405,606,683 yuan, an increase of 679,250,019 yuan compared to the previous year's 8,726,356,664 yuan. Excluding the 200,000,000 yuan increase in debt, pensions, and retirement allowances, the net increase in national expenditure for 1940-41 is approximately 500,000,000 yuan. It is estimated that the national tax revenue for 1940-41 can offset 3,274,428,817 yuan of general expenditure and 783,000,000 yuan of special emergency military expenditure items, totaling 4,057,428,817 yuan. There is still a shortage of 5,348,177,866 yuan. It is now planned to use 1,671,177,866 yuan in public bonds to make up for the special expenditure, and 3,677,000,000 yuan in public bonds to make up for the shortage in special emergency military expenditure items. The amount obtained from public bonds in 1939-40 totaled 5,651,803,155 yuan. Although the amount for 1940-41 is 303,625,289 yuan less than this amount, it is still very large. It is expected that additional budgets will be submitted in the future, so the number of bonds to be issued now seems likely to continue to increase. As for the projected increase in national tax revenue, before deducting various items, it is estimated that 4,151,784,437 yuan can be collected, an increase of 1,074,973,637 yuan compared to the estimated 3,076,810,800 yuan for 1939-40. The largest item of income, ordinary and special taxes, can reach 901,736,451 yuan. The second largest is that revenue from government undertakings and industries can increase by 82,020,827 yuan, the main item being the tobacco monopoly. The third type is relatively small, with stamp duty revenue estimated at 16,356,040 yuan. (February 22, Reuter's dispatch)

Japan and Argentina Engage in Economic Talks; Japan Attempts to Find New Markets 29

Paris - Representatives from Japan and Argentina began economic talks in Tokyo this morning. Well-informed sources here recently stated that the French government is paying close attention to this matter. The goal of Japan's move is to find new markets so that it no longer has to rely on the United States. After the Japanese-American commercial treaty expired on January 26 of this year, although trade between Japan and the United States still maintains its original status, it is no longer protected by the treaty. The US government can implement embargo measures against Japan at any time. This means that Japan relies on American goods for both its continued war against China and its domestic economic life. The Japanese government has tried to express its sincerity to the United States with the promise to open the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, in order to urge it to re-sign the commercial treaty. However, the US government still considers this road insufficient and has no intention of re-signing the commercial treaty. As a result, commerce between Japan and the United States has fallen into a treaty-less state, and the proposal to open the Yangtze River has been postponed until now due to the need for a decision by the Japanese military authorities. At this point, the Japanese government has changed its commercial policy, attempting to find another way for the goods currently sold to the United States, transporting them to Latin American markets for sale, and purchasing the raw materials it needs from other places. Taking Argentina as an example, Japan purchased goods worth 42 million pesos from the country in 1936, while its exports to the country were worth 26 million pesos, resulting in a trade deficit of 16 million pesos, which has been increasing. Japan is now eager to sign an agreement with Argentina for political reasons. Therefore, Argentina is in a very good position in the current talks. (February 21, Havas dispatch)

Japanese Asia Development Board Formulates Principles for Businesses in China; Raw Materials Must Not Solely Rely on Supply from Japan 30

Tokyo - According to the Asahi Shimbun, the Asia Development Board has formulated several principles to determine what types of Japanese industry and commerce may be operated in China. Businesses that rely solely on the supply of raw materials from Japan will not be allowed to establish themselves in China, in order to maintain the supply of Japanese raw materials such as coal and copper for domestic needs and avoid the coal shortages that Japan currently has. To prevent conflicts between the Japanese domestic industrial world and Japanese entrepreneurs in China, the Asia Development Board will not allow the operation in China of businesses that are already operating in Japan. All new businesses will be limited to those that do not compete with Japanese industry. However, this should not be interpreted as meaning that Japanese cotton and silk spinning industries should not expand in China. It is heard that any factories established in China in the future will be built in the industrial areas designated in the new Shanghai city plan. The Asia Development Board has also decided to carefully monitor and prevent the advancement of Japanese businesses in China from conflicting with the interests of Chinese people in the territory. The Asahi Shimbun speculates that the North China Development Company plans to move its main offices to Beiping and Zhangjiakou instead of Tokyo, as proposed by the company's president, Kaya. It is said that if the plan approved by the Asia Development Board is implemented, two-thirds of the company's president, vice president, directors, and 200 Tokyo office staff will move to Beiping and Zhangjiakou. (February 22, Reuter's dispatch)

Three Britons Arrested in Kobe; Question Raised in British House of Commons 31

London - The House of Commons held a meeting this afternoon, and a member asked about the arrest of three British subjects in Kobe, Japan. Undersecretary of State for Foreign Affairs Butler replied, "Foreign Secretary Halifax has received a report stating that one of the three is Reverend Walters, an Australian national who is in charge of the Seamen's Mission in Kobe. The other two, named Griffiths and Peters, were arrested on the 17th of last month. The Japanese side has not yet officially announced the reason for their arrest. Our Consul-General in Kobe, Owens, has visited them twice. The Foreign Office is in contact with our Ambassador to Japan, Sir Craigie, regarding this matter." (February 21, Havas dispatch)

The Altmark Case: Britain and Norway Continue Negotiations; Seeking to Prevent Germany from Exploiting Neutral Territorial Waters; Switzerland Feels similarly Entangled 32

London – Regarding the "Altmark" case, well-informed sources here say that Foreign Secretary Halifax recently met with Norwegian Minister Colban, posing several questions and awaiting a formal response. Therefore, the British government does not intend to reply to the arguments put forward by Norwegian Foreign Minister Koht in the House of Commons the other day. However, in practice, regardless of Norway's arguments, the British government has ample words to defend itself. The Royal Navy's actions are fully justified in law, and Britain's current position is beyond reproach. Moreover, British public opinion fully supports the government's actions, giving the government even more confidence. As for France, its position has been clearly stated and is entirely consistent with that of the British government. In short, Germany's exploitation of the weakness of various neutral countries is not new. The current issue is to decide on appropriate measures to prevent Germany from continuing to exploit the territorial waters of neutral countries. (Havas, 21st)

Oslo – The 'Norwegian Telegraph Agency' yesterday published a statement by Foreign Minister Koht, stating that when Britain and Norway held talks in the summer of 1939, the British government solemnly declared that warships should have the right to enter Norwegian territorial waters and remain there indefinitely. The British government claimed that this principle was recognized by all countries. Koht continued, saying that international law only recognizes two types of ships: warships and merchant ships. The 'government ships' such as the Altmark should be regarded as warships and enjoy the rights of warships recognized by the British government, including the right to freely pass through the territorial waters of neutral countries. (Haitong, 22nd)

Berlin – Regarding the British destroyer 'Cossack' attacking the German ship 'Altmark', German newspapers and political figures continue to discuss the matter. Newspapers hint that Germany will retaliate sooner or later for this British act of violence, but officials decline to answer this question. (Haitong, 22nd)

London – According to a special dispatch from here today, Italian newspapers carried a London telegram regarding the "Altmark" incident, stating, "Although Britain and Norway currently have a dispute, good relations between the two countries will not be disturbed." The Montevideo Plata newspaper commented on the "Altmark" case with the headline, "Landing on the Altmark to avoid a flight; from a humanitarian point of view, this matter should be congratulated." The Swiss National Newspaper stated, "The Norwegian Parliament's allowing others to disrespect Norwegian neutrality has caused great concern. Switzerland is now facing a similarly complex task, but despite various speeches, the Altmark incident was actually caused by Norway's misunderstanding of its neutral duties. The British destroyer's resolute action has given Germany a warning, hoping that Germany will recognize that it no longer has the freedom in neutral territorial waters as it does at home, and that Norway will take more effective precautions to prevent a recurrence of unfortunate incidents." (Reuters, 22nd)

Foreign Ministers' Meeting of Three Nordic Countries Scheduled to Begin Tomorrow 33

Copenhagen – Government newspapers recently reported that the foreign ministers of the Scandinavian countries, namely Denmark, Sweden, and Norway, are scheduled to hold a meeting here on the 24th and 25th of this month. The agenda includes: (1) various serious problems encountered by the Nordic neutral countries in the current European war; (2) naval battles conducted by the belligerent countries; (3) the war being waged by a fraternal Nordic country, namely Finland; and (4) the economic policies to be implemented by the Nordic countries. It is generally expected that as a result of this meeting, the Scandinavian countries will not find it difficult to decide on various measures in the hope of jointly alleviating or avoiding the current difficulties. (Havas, 23rd)

British Newspapers Report: Situation in the Near East; Close Contact between Turkey, Britain, and France 34

London – Today, the political correspondent of the Daily Telegraph stated that it is now known that the Soviet Union has begun to exert its influence in the Near East. Bajera Town Bombed; Sweden Protests to the Soviet Union; Discussion also Raised in British House of Commons; No Intention to Mediate the Soviet-Finnish War 35

Sweden – Seven Soviet aircraft flew over the Swedish town of Bajera today afternoon (ten kilometers from the Finnish border) and bombed it indiscriminately, setting the entire town on fire. The Swedish ambassador to the Soviet Union has been ordered to lodge a strong protest with the Soviet authorities. According to the latest news, the Soviet aircraft flew to Bajera Town at 1:00 p.m. today, from a height of three or four thousand meters, dropping a total of fifty bombs and hundreds of incendiary bombs, most of which landed in the central area, destroying many houses and immediately starting fires. The material losses are very heavy. Another ten or so bombs landed near a church, destroying a sawmill. Fortunately, the workers had all fled, and there were no casualties. Afterwards, the aircraft flew towards Finland. (Havas, 21st)

Stockholm – The Swedish Foreign Minister has instructed the ambassador to Moscow to lodge a strong protest regarding the bombing of Bajera village, five miles outside the Finnish border within Swedish territory, by Soviet aircraft. It is heard that the village was hit by ten high-explosive bombs and several incendiary bombs, resulting in the burning of four houses and damage to a church. The main road is also said to have been damaged, but there were no casualties among the residents. (Reuters, 22nd)

Oslo – According to news from Stockholm, after the Soviet bombing of Bajera Town yesterday, General Nygren, commander of the northern defense district of that country, recently reiterated his previous order, instructing troops stationed in various locations to use anti-aircraft guns to fire on foreign aircraft when they intrude, without leniency. (Havas, 22nd)

Stockholm – Swedish newspapers have expressed outrage at yesterday's bombing of Bajera village by Soviet aircraft. The Ny Tid newspaper stated that Sweden will not only demand compensation from the Soviet Union but also ask the Soviet side to order its air force personnel to avoid such incidents in the future. The Dagens Nyheter newspaper also stated that the Soviet move was a shocking violation of neutrality and a precedent in the history of aerial warfare. (Reuters, 22nd)

London – Yesterday, a question was raised in the British House of Commons regarding the Soviet bombing. Under-Secretary of State Butler replied that the Soviet Air Force's policy of indiscriminate bombing was reprehensible, but the British government had not lodged a protest because, unfortunately, there was no reason to believe that British action could produce the results it hoped for. Labour MP Hyndman asked whether Prime Minister Chamberlain would consider contacting the League of Nations or President Roosevelt in order to mediate the Soviet-Finnish conflict. Butler replied that the League of Nations had intervened to mediate on December 12th, which Finland had accepted, but the Soviet Union had rejected. The Soviet and Finnish governments may request or accept mediation by a third country at any time, but the British government has no right to engage in participation between the governments of a third country and the two belligerent countries. (Reuters, 21st)

Stockholm – It is declared here that Soviet Russian Ambassador to Sweden, Madame Kollontai, on behalf of the Soviet government, informed the Swedish Foreign Minister that after the Russian army conquers Finland, it will not advance into Sweden. (Haitong, 22nd)

German Aircraft Fly Over Dutch Airspace; Netherlands Formally Protests to Germany; Foreign Aircraft also Discovered in Belgian Territory 36

The Hague – Several German aircraft flew over Dutch airspace yesterday. The Dutch government has formally protested. Regarding this matter, the Government Information Bureau recently stated that a total of five German aircraft passed through Winterswijk, Sittard, Middelburg, De Cocksdorp, and Zundert yesterday. One of them in De Cocksdorp was fired upon by our anti-aircraft artillery. Another was driven away by our patrol aircraft in the provinces of Friesland and Groningen. Afterwards, the government lodged a protest with the German government. Also, last night, machine gun fire and anti-aircraft gun fire were heard in eight locations in our country. It is not yet known whether these aircraft belong to Britain or Germany. The government has inquired with both the British and German governments to investigate. (Havas, 21st)

The Hague – Officials announce that Dutch anti-aircraft artillery near Heiloo last night opened fire on foreign aircraft of unknown nationality. (Reuters, 22nd)

Berlin – Responsible parties here told foreign reporters yesterday that the London radio report that German aircraft flew into Dutch territory and were fired upon by Dutch anti-aircraft artillery was inaccurate. A German official spokesperson declared that the aircraft shot at in Dutch territory were likely British aircraft because British aircraft often fly over Dutch territory when attempting to fly to Heligoland Bight. (Haitong, 22nd)

Liège, Belgium – An aircraft of unknown nationality flew to Liège, Belgium, today. The local anti-aircraft artillery opened fire, and after pursuit by a fighter plane, it flew eastward. (Havas, 21st)

Soviet Union Decides to Launch Large-Scale Offensive on Mannerheim Line; Karelian Finnish Shorten Lines; Large Numbers of British Aircraft and War Materiel Shipped to Finland 37

Moscow – According to the official TASS news agency, the Red Army has decided to launch a large-scale offensive to break through the Mannerheim Line, and the Finnish war can be brought to an end in this offensive. However, due to the solidity of the Mannerheim Line, which is no less than the Maginot and Siegfried Lines, this task may not be easy. There will be fierce battles near Vyborg. Soviet journalists believe that on the Red Army's 22nd anniversary tomorrow, the Soviet army will make progress in that area. TASS stated that the Red Army is gradually becoming familiar with the terrain and climate and will soon launch a large-scale offensive. (United Press, 22nd)

Stockholm – According to a Moscow correspondent for a newspaper here, Soviet Naval Commissar Kuznetsov is said to have flown to Murmansk. The entire Soviet fleet in the Arctic Ocean is now preparing for action. (Reuters, 22nd)

Helsinki – After the Finnish army retreated to the northern line, the entire Karelian line moved. According to the latest news, the Soviet army has advanced towards the new Finnish line. (Haitong, 22nd)

Helsinki – Regarding the fighting on the Karelian front, the Red Army originally hoped to break through the Mannerheim Line and seize the port of Vyborg on the 23rd (the 22nd anniversary of the founding of the Red Army), but the Finnish army has only retreated six kilometers so far and continues to resist stubbornly. In addition, in recent days, the Finnish army has abandoned several positions in Karelia, and the lines have been shortened, making them easier to defend. In addition, when retreating, the original positions were destroyed, and it will take the Red Army a long time to repair them. Therefore, the Red Army's hope of capturing Vyborg soon has been dashed. The lines currently held by the Finnish army are stronger than those abandoned. Red Army aircraft are heavily bombing the area, with the city of Riihimäki being the most heavily bombed. (Havas, 22nd)

Moscow – According to a communiqué from the headquarters of the Leningrad Military District, yesterday, in air combat, the Soviet Air Force shot down sixteen enemy aircraft and bombed enemy troops and military targets. As for the front lines, from the 19th to the 21st, Soviet troops occupied the Joensuu fortress area and 176 fortresses, including 37 solid gun emplacements. (TASS, 22nd)

Helsinki – Finnish communiqués stated that in yesterday's air battles, the Finnish side shot down seventeen Soviet aircraft. The Finnish Air Force flew over Soviet lines to conduct reconnaissance and bombed Soviet concentrations several times. Yesterday, the Soviet army launched increasingly frequent attacks in Karelia, but they were all repelled. The Soviet side suffered heavy losses and destroyed many tanks. (Reuters, 22nd)

Helsinki – Fifty Soviet aircraft bombed Ivalo and Rovaniemi in Petsamo this morning, causing heavy losses. The Soviet aircraft then flew southwest. (Haitong, 22nd)

London – The Finnish embassy's call for foreign volunteers has aroused great concern and excitement among the people of London and the United Kingdom. It is heard that some people have enlisted, especially those skilled in skiing and mountaineering. In addition, according to reliable sources, the material assistance that Britain is shipping to Finland is also quite substantial. Reuters has learned that 144 aircraft, including 120 fighter planes and 24 bombers, are en route to Finland, with about 40 or 50 already arriving in Finland. A large amount of war materiel and ammunition is also being shipped to Finland, including 150 flat-shooting rifles and ammunition, 10,000 anti-tank mines, 50,000 hand grenades, 15 howitzers, 100 machine guns and ammunition, 24 anti-aircraft guns and shells, 30 field guns, four six-ton tanks, twelve six-inch guns and shells, and ten three-inch mortars and shells. Non-lethal military supplies, such as gas masks, tents, clothing, and telephones, have also been shipped in large quantities. (Reuters, 22nd)

Paris – Ten thousand Hungarian volunteers willing to fight for Finland have arrived, with the first batch of about one thousand arriving here last night. According to Le Parisien, they will depart for London today. Many of them are veterans, and some are officers, all fully armed. Their commander stated that they received a very friendly welcome when they passed through Yugoslavia and Italy. (Reuters, 22nd)

Ankara – According to news received here, the pro-British policies of the Said government were the reason for the army's resentment, leading to the government's resignation. The Iraqi interim government, under pressure from Britain, has decided to dismiss General Fazi, Chief of Staff, General Osman, commander of the First Division, and Colonel Yamulk, commander of the mechanized forces. German Pocket Battleship Lying in Wait to Attack Merchant Ships; Seeking Revenge for the Graf Spee in the South Atlantic; Britain Accelerates Arming of All Ships 39

Montevideo – La Democracia reports, citing responsible sources, that a German pocket battleship, either the Deutschland or the Admiral Scheer, is now lying in wait in the South Atlantic to attack merchant ships and avenge the Graf Spee. Recent dispatches claim that the German freighter La Plata, bound for Buenos Aires, will likely serve as the supply ship for the pocket battleship. The Deutschland and Admiral Scheer are sister ships of the Graf Spee, which was recently scuttled after engaging three British cruisers. Each weighs 10,000 tons, has a speed of 26 knots, is equipped with six 11-inch guns and eight 6-inch guns, and is said to have a cruising range of 10,000 miles. Both are equipped with diesel engines. (Reuters, 22nd)

London – First Lord of the Admiralty Churchill reported to the House of Commons last night, at the request of members, on the latest details of the British effort to combat German submarines, stating that British success against German submarines was greater than expected. The German side sometimes intensifies its actions against world merchant ships, and sometimes withdraws its submarines for inspection, rest, or repair. Therefore, the results of British resistance will naturally vary from week to week. However, the success in recent weeks shows that the German submarine sinking rate he mentioned in the House of Commons last December was by no means an exaggeration. The First Lord later reiterated in response to questions that the government intends to arm all ships, including fishing boats, as quickly as possible, and that a strong air patrol will be established to protect fishing boats. Churchill stated in the House of Commons on December 6th that the destruction of German submarines was proceeding as usual and was consistent with his previous estimate, namely a sinking rate of two to four per week, and he believes that this sinking rate is higher than Germany's replenishment capacity. (Reuters, 22nd)

Continued Losses of Ships of Various Nationalities

Rotterdam – Two Dutch ships, the 4,760-ton steamer Tera and the 8,970-ton motor tanker Den Haag, have become the latest victims of the European war. The Tera exploded and sank yesterday about sixty miles southwest of Finisterre. At the time, the ship was carrying grain for the Dutch government and was sailing from Argentina back to Rotterdam. The cause of the explosion is unknown. The captain and crew have been rescued. The Den Haag, carrying 11,000 tons of oil products from New York to Rotterdam, has been overdue for a long time and has not yet arrived in port, so it is feared that it has been lost en route. It is widely believed that the Spanish Pendulas (2,000 tons), which sank six miles off Cape Villano on Sunday due to an explosion, was sunk by a German submarine. Twenty-two of the twenty-nine crew members were lost. According to the latest information, the Norwegian ship Steinstad, weighing 2,476 tons, which was torpedoed off the coast of Ireland on February 15th, had eleven crew members who drifted in lifeboats for five days and finally landed on an island on Tuesday. The remaining thirteen are feared to have drowned. (Reuters, 22nd)

The Hague – The Dutch fishing boat Barendsz (250 tons) recently struck a mine in the North Sea and sank. All crew members were rescued by other fishing boats. (Havas, 21st)

Oslo – According to today's announcement, Norway has lost a total of 49 ships, totaling 168,527 tons. A total of 327 Norwegians have died. (Reuters, 22nd)

London – The Air Ministry stated that just after noon today, an enemy aircraft was shot down by a British fighter plane near the northeast coast of Britain. Another, a Heinkel bomber, was attacked by a Spitfire fighter plane from the Coastal Command and was destroyed on land near St. Abbs Head in Scotland. (Reuters, 22nd)

Copenhagen – The Danish Ministry of Commerce recently issued an order stipulating that Danish ships may not sail alone in the North Sea unless accompanied by ships from other neutral countries. This restriction does not apply to those sailing to distant overseas locations and sailing north of 61 degrees north latitude. (Havas, 21st)

Stockholm – The Executive Committee of the Swedish Seamen's Union recently passed a resolution stating that the naval warfare methods of the belligerent countries are inhumane and should not be used. Ye Chuchang Urges People in the Rear to Strive to be Friends of the Wounded Soldiers; Foster Your Enthusiasm and Cherish the Wounded Soldiers Even More 40

Chongqing – Secretary-General Ye Chuchang recently published an article entitled "Strive to be Friends of the Wounded Soldiers" as follows: The destiny of the nation and the people rests on the loyal and brave soldiers at the front. The lives and property of the compatriots in the rear depend entirely on the destiny of the nation. The loyal and brave soldiers at the front not only support the destiny of the nation but also protect the lives and property of the compatriots in the rear. Who does not love life and hate death? Who has no parents and no brothers? The soldiers at the front have taken on such great responsibilities, resolved to die and forget life, abandoning parents and brothers, building a great wall for the destiny of the nation, and becoming a guarantee for the lives and property of the compatriots. Grateful and knowing, drinking water and thinking of the source, speaking of reason, asking conscience, how should we, the ordinary compatriots in the rear, strive to repay the soldiers at the front? Therefore, their bodies are injured, their health is lost, they toss and turn on their sickbeds, and they are taken into hospitals. How should we appreciate and repay their heroic spirit and painful situation? The same nationals should bear the same responsibilities. If labor and leisure are different, and sweetness and bitterness are uneven, how can we comfort our conscience? Therefore, when we wear clothes, we should think of the cold wind and severe frost, thick snow and hard ice at the front. When we eat, we should think of the soldiers at the front enduring hunger and thirst, and fighting hard. When family members gather together, we should think of the soldiers at the front facing strong enemies and leaving their hometowns to fight to the death with the enemy. We should send them the most enthusiastic and noblest sympathy and reward. The purpose of launching the "Friends of the Wounded Soldiers" movement is to enable every compatriot in the rear to foster their enthusiasm and cherish those heroic soldiers who are injured on the front lines even more. When we do our best to love and care for the wounded soldiers, we are exercising our utmost sincerity and fulfilling our duty. Under the leadership of the President of our Party, the War of Resistance has been going on for three years. The power and arrogance of the Japanese have declined by eighty or ninety percent. Now, the Japanese army, society, and even the Diet are filled with war-weariness, mutual complaints, and mutual hostility. Therefore, our victory depends entirely on whether we subjectively want it, not on whether the Japanese objectively can. If we can show the nation's internal love and sincerity and its increasingly courageous spirit in fighting the enemy, the Japanese will certainly not be able to reverse their misfortune and support their aggressive actions. The loyal and brave soldiers at the front have demonstrated their increasingly courageous strength, and the compatriots in the rear must also demonstrate their loving and sincere strength. The exertion of this strength should not only be used on the soldiers at the front but also on the families of the soldiers, so that the soldiers at the front have no worries about their families. This is a natural responsibility for the compatriots in the rear. It must be known that this is not our favor to the soldiers at the front; it is only a very small reward for the soldiers at the front. However, when this small reward is launched nationwide, it will become a great contribution to the country. The significance of our recruitment of friends of the wounded soldiers is not only to hope that every compatriot can be a close friend of the wounded heroes but also to be brothers to the wounded soldiers. We must be able to take care of the families of the soldiers at the front, just as older brothers go out to fight and younger brothers take care of the family. Those who have money should contribute money, and those who have strength should contribute strength. The people of the whole country know that this is the responsibility that everyone should fulfill during the War of Resistance. However, this only asks us to contribute money if we have surplus money and strength if we have surplus strength, not to give up our own lives and families to contribute money and strength. Now, the soldiers fighting at the front and the wounded brothers are truly disregarding their own lives and families to protect the lives and families of their compatriots. Even if we do not consider the nation and the people, but only consider our own lives and property, we should have a kind of enthusiastic sympathy and reward for them. For example, when robbers break into our gate, and brave men come out and drive away the robbers, but they are injured, can we not give the warriors who were injured defending us warm love and reward? This war of resistance is not only related to the survival of our nation, but also to the survival of our descendants in the future, and to the survival of our ancestors' sacrifices in the past. Our thousands of years of national spirit is to be kind to our descendants and filial to our ancestors. The injured brothers have done their best for our kindness and filial piety, and sacrificed their healthy limbs. If we can be virtuous parents and filial sons and virtuous grandchildren in our families, we must give the most and greatest reward to these loyal and brave wounded soldiers so that we will not be ashamed of our ancestors and future generations. The comrades of our party, influenced by the teachings of the late Premier and the instructions of the President, have deeply remembered the four words of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, and love. In this time of national crisis, being able to exert more of the spirit of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, and love means fulfilling more of the responsibility of our party members and strengthening the foundation of the party and the country. The launch of the Friends of the Wounded Soldiers movement is based on this spirit. Therefore, this recruitment of friends of the wounded soldiers can be regarded as a measure of the morality and strength of our party members. The wounded soldiers have done their best to fulfill their aspirations and skills of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, and love for the nation. We, the compatriots in the rear, living in a relatively safe place, should remember the lesson that "when the nest is overturned, no egg remains intact," and thus not forget the great personality and suffering of the wounded heroes. Only in this way can we avoid creating the pain of national subjugation and extinction. The pain of killing enemies and achieving results is glorious, but the pain of national subjugation and extinction is not only tragic but also a great shame for the compatriots across the country. If we want to avoid this tragic great shame, we must all work hard to love and care for the wounded heroes and reward the wounded heroes and their families with the greatest enthusiasm. (21st dispatch)

Foreign Trade in Fujian Province After the War: Exports Have Not Increased, Imports Have Gradually Decreased 41

Fuzhou Correspondence: The state of foreign trade in Fujian Province in recent years can be represented by the import and export figures of various ports. The total tonnage of ships entering and leaving the ports in 1938 and the total tonnage of ships entering and leaving the ports in 1934, when the total value of trade in the three years before the war was highest, have not changed much. It can be seen that in 1938 after the war, there was still little impact. However, the total value of foreign trade in Fujian Province has been gradually declining since 1935, often between 80 million and 90 million yuan. The long-term trade deficit has fallen from more than 30 million yuan to 9 million yuan, a significant decrease, which seems to be a good sign. However, according to the statistics of recent years, this good sign seems to be true and false. Because exports have not increased, while imports have gradually decreased. After the two have been offset, the trade deficit has decreased. In the past five years, except for 1937, when exports rose slightly, merchants accelerated the sale of goods when the war just started and traffic was cut off, which was a temporary stimulus. Other periods changed very little. International imports were more than 24 million yuan in 1934, and decreased by 25% after the war. Inter-provincial imports were more than 47 million yuan in 1934, and decreased by 50% after the war. This is the main reason for the suppression of the entire trade deficit. In fact, inter-provincial trade has declined. In terms of the percentage of international and inter-provincial trade deficits, 1938 reached a ratio of 85 to 15. Therefore, the flexible international trade and the exchange of local products for provincial needs should not be ignored. As for the shift in the order of import and export commodities, rice, cotton cloth, wheat flour, and fertilizer have always occupied the top few import positions, while tea, paper, wood, dried and fresh fruits, and sugar have always occupied the top few export positions. Now, although the harassment of Japanese warships has affected foreign trade, purchases and sales can still be made from neighboring provinces of Zhejiang and Jiangxi to promote the prosperity of inter-provincial trade. Regarding the analysis of international trade, trade with Japan and its colonies was more than 6.9 million yuan in 1935, while in 1938, the wartime reaction was fully demonstrated, decreasing to an unprecedented low of more than 300,000 yuan (all imported from Xiamen after its fall). Imports from other countries such as the United Kingdom and the United States have increased slightly. Hong Kong has jumped from a trade deficit to a trade surplus, which is due to the centralized export of local products.

Suzhou Fishing Industry is Again Controlled by Japanese Merchants 42

Taijiu Company Has Resumed Business

Suzhou Correspondence: Fish and shrimp aquatic products in this county are known for being abundant. The annual sales volume is very large. After the fall, ordinary fish merchants were unable to achieve the smooth sales of the pre-war period due to Japanese restrictions, and the overall business was greatly inferior. In the winter of the year before last, the Japanese, in view of the need for fish and shrimp in Shanghai, superficially organized the Taijiu Industry Company in cooperation with the Japanese puppets. On the one hand, it controlled the fish, shrimp, and vegetables in Suzhou, and on the other hand, it forced the purchase of fish and shrimp from fishmongers connected to Shanghai, and then sold them to the Shanghai market in the name of the company. A year ago, the Japanese ordered the company to stop business due to staff embezzlement. At that time, the original fish merchants heard the news and all cheered, believing that they could get rid of Japanese shackles. It is cursed that the company resumed business on the 15th of this month. It is heard that the scope of business has been expanded, and not only fish and shrimp but also famous products throughout Suzhou will be manipulated. Therefore, merchants in this county can be said to be in a desperate situation.

The Four Townships of Kunshan Have Become a World of Bandits 43

Farmers Suffer the Most

Kunshan Correspondence: Recently, bandits have been rampant in the four townships of the county. This is because the pseudo-Pacification Team of the county was ordered by the pseudo-Provincial Security Team last autumn to go to Lumu area of Wuxian County to assist the Japanese army in attacking the guerrillas. This pseudo-Pacification Team was originally reorganized from bandits and had no combat capability at all. Therefore, once they encountered the guerrillas, they collapsed at the mere sight of them without even fighting, and all the guns were confiscated. They fled back one after another. After these people sneaked back to their hometowns, they certainly could not live in peace, and the villages have not been able to rest peacefully since then. Pseudo-squad leaders such as Xu and Lu in the northwest township of the county have many followers. After escaping from Lumu, they openly used the name of burning lucky money to widely distribute invitation cards to the people to collect money. It is heard that the gift money is divided into three types: fortune, wealth, and longevity. The "fortune" character is 20 yuan, the "wealth" character is 10 yuan, and the "longevity" character is 5 yuan. What kind of gift money should be sent by what kind of family has been designated by them. Any household that receives an invitation card does not dare to send it. However, this is still extortion by officials. Robbery and kidnapping happen almost every day, and they are often committed by these people. The most severely affected are often farmers. Because farmers rely on farming for a living, are attached to their land and reluctant to move, and live scattered in villages and cannot defend themselves. However, the bandits' purpose is to rob legal tender, rice, wheat, etc. Even a pig or a chicken cannot be spared. Even cattle are coveted by bandits. If the farmers' cattle are robbed, they cannot afford to buy them back and will have nothing to cultivate. Therefore, during the slack season, they take them to nearby towns to be fostered by people. However, the spring plowing season is approaching, and in fact, they have to take the cattle back for cultivation. They are also afraid of being robbed again. The suffering they endure is hard to describe. The reason why bandits dare to be so rampant is that they collude with the pseudo-organizations.

The detective team of the Father Pseudo Police Station takes the opportunity to extort money under the guise of searching for guns. As for their methods, they use local ruffians as their ears and eyes, ordering them to falsely report wealthy farmers as hiding guns. When the person is arrested, someone is sent to his home to bargain. As a result, the matter is settled with a fine. Countless people have been victimized. It is heard that a Zhu in the northwest township has been reported to hide guns as many as four times, and the total amount of fines has reached more than 3,000 yuan. Everyone who has some wealth is in danger.

Tang Dynasty Arhat Sculptures from Baosheng Temple in Jiaozhi are Shipped Eastward 44

Rare Antiques Taken Away by the Japanese Army, Only Four Remain, and It Is Still Difficult to Ensure Their Preservation

Kunshan Correspondence: The Arhat statues in Baosheng Temple in Jiaozhi were sculpted by Yang Huizhi of the Tang Dynasty. Yang was a master of ancient Chinese sculpture art. After the Taiping Rebellion, eight statues and some broken pieces of murals remained. Previously, Gu Jiegang wrote an article about them, which was published in the "Short Story Monthly," which aroused the research interest of Japanese writer Nishiya Omura. When he traveled to China, he personally went to the temple to take videos and add explanations, forming a book called "Remnants of Murals." Because of this, artists from all over the world have paid close attention to it. Whenever they come to China, they must visit the temple. Later, Ye Gongchuo, Jiang Xiaojian, and others, together with the Jiangsu Provincial Government, organized the Jiaozhi Baosheng Temple Tang Sculpture Preservation Committee to repair the remaining eight Arhats and piece together the broken pieces of Yuntao murals. On the day of the completion, people from all walks of life went to visit, thinking that these only remaining eight Tang sculptures would be permanently preserved and would no longer be lost. However, since the fall of the counties in southern Jiangsu, the Baosheng Temple has been stationed by Japanese troops. The Tang sculptures in the temple have long been noticed by them. They have specifically transported four of the most vivid statues back to their country as antiques. Now, only four statues remain. It is still difficult to predict whether the last four remaining statues can be preserved.

Education News

Issues of Adjusting Vocational Education and Education in Pudong, China (1) 45

– Cheng Qibao

Since its inception, although China's school system has been revised several times, it has never deviated from the legacy of the past imperial examination education. It focuses on general training, while vocational education is only a by-product of educational facilities. In other words, China's school system is purely centered on liberal arts education, and its methods and teaching materials are all aimed at preparing students for further education. However, in reality, under today's social conditions, even if education has developed to a considerable degree, the number of people preparing for further education is still extremely small. Most children and young people, those who have not received education are not worth mentioning, even those who have received education cannot continue their studies and have no special skills in production, thus becoming an extremely serious problem in society. Today, general opinions are focused on this when expressing dissatisfaction with education, thus causing the orthodox debate between general education and vocational education.

Objectively speaking, education really contains the meaning of production. If education cannot give the educated a considerable amount of production skills, it will lose its basic function. China's school system is based on general training, and at the same time, people in society still have the feudal thought of "getting promoted and making a fortune," which is the malady of education for decades. Today's problem is not who is orthodox between general education and vocational education, but how to harmonize them, a kind of education, to complete a rational school system. For example, primary school is education shared by the general public. Basic national training must be available. According to other countries, after the completion of this basic national training, those who can continue their studies continue their studies, and those who need to produce produce, each has its own track and development, which is the most appropriate strategy. However, it is difficult to do so in China due to social and economic conditions and the reality of educational facilities. One must find other remedies. That is, in the class where children receive basic education, they must be given considerable vocational training at the same time (the author has advocated that the age of enrollment for ordinary children, especially rural children, should be delayed to ten years, so that at least after graduating from junior primary school, they can also engage in a profession according to their physiological and psychological development). They do not have to wait until after graduating from primary school to be given vocational training. According to this method, the curriculum, teaching materials, and teaching methods of today's primary schools must be fundamentally transformed to be able to proceed smoothly. As for middle schools, they are places for excellent children selected from primary schools to study in depth. They are training institutions for a small number of people. Those who are able to continue their studies can enter ordinary middle schools through assessment and testing (this kind of middle school does not need to be expanded excessively, one should base it on needs. However, on the quality side, one must strictly advocate strictness). Other children should be sent to various vocational schools to create a tenth-level cadre talent who is self-sufficient and self-reliant in society. As for universities or specialized schools, they are training institutions for a very small number of outstanding young people. Their departments should be widely established. The purpose is to create real leaders in society, and one should not allow unqualified people to increase the waste of education. (The End)

Zhejiang Province's Wartime People's School Implements Compulsory Enrollment Measures 47

(Fangyan Correspondence) The Zhejiang Provincial Government Committee has approved and filed the implementation of compulsory enrollment measures for wartime people's schools in Zhejiang Province. The full text of these measures is extracted below: Article 1: These measures are formulated in accordance with the "Provisional Measures for Compulsory Enrollment of Out-of-School People in Provinces and Cities" promulgated by the Ministry of Education. Article 2: Each wartime people's school (hereinafter referred to as wartime people's school) should first print and distribute a survey form for out-of-school people before implementing compulsory enrollment of out-of-school people. The form should be handed over to the township and village chiefs in the area to complete the survey of out-of-school adults aged 16 to 35 within the shortest possible time as a basis for implementation. Article 3: All out-of-school people, regardless of gender, occupation, or origin, should be compulsorily enrolled, except for those who are mentally ill, have chronic diseases, or are deaf-mutes or disabled and have been verified as such. Out-of-school people aged 16 to 25 should be enrolled first, followed by out-of-school people aged 26 to 35. They should be assigned in batches by the township and village chiefs in the area. If the people who should be enrolled are temporarily unable to enroll due to illness, with the village chief's verification and the evidence, they will be allowed to postpone their enrollment and will be ordered to enroll after they recover their health. Article 4: The compulsory enrollment period for out-of-school people is set at two months, with two hours of lessons per day. Article 5: Out-of-school people should go to school on time every day after being assigned to enroll and must not evade. Article 6: If out-of-school people fail to go to school as assigned or are often absent, the school may handle it according to the following procedures: (1) verbal or oral advice; (2) written or oral warning; (3) request the local district office or police agency to send police to summon them to school; (4) request the local district office or police agency to impose a fine of 3 cents to 1.5 yuan, or labor service of 1 to 3 days; (5) if the absence exceeds one-third of the teaching period, they must still be enrolled in the second phase. Article 7: For out-of-school people of an employed nature, employers must not use this as an excuse to prevent them from enrolling during the compulsory enrollment period, or deduct their wages due to their enrollment. If the above situation occurs, the school may write to the local district office or police agency to give the employer a warning or fine, depending on the circumstances, and still order him to allow the workers to enroll and not dismiss them on the pretext. Article 8: After enrolling, out-of-school people should actively participate in the school's extracurricular activities and wartime rear work, and must not evade without reason. Article 9: If people who have already enrolled change their address, they should ask the original school to issue a transfer certificate and continue to receive education at the wartime people's school in the relocated area. Article 10: These measures are formulated by the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education and submitted to the Zhejiang Provincial Government for approval and implementation.

French Concession Determined to Suppress Commodity Prices: Municipal Council Considers Measures; Trade Associations Investigate Inventory Quantities; Four Banks Agree to Provide Funds for Fair-Price Purchase and Sale; Speculators Should Repent Quickly 59

The French Concession authorities, in order to safeguard the livelihood of the common people, have taken the lead in organizing a committee to be solely responsible for investigating commodity prices, setting fair prices, ensuring impartiality, and benefiting both production and consumption. Those who manipulate the market for profit will be strictly prosecuted in accordance with the "Emergency Period Commodity Price Assessment and Anti-Speculation Measures" promulgated by the National Government on February 20 of last year. Since this news was revealed by this newspaper, all sectors have praised and rejoiced upon hearing it. The Shanghai Municipal Council is also considering a similar plan. Shanghai's trade associations also plan to conduct inventory quantity surveys for various industries to stabilize prices. With the Concession authorities and trade associations advancing simultaneously, the effect will be significant and will greatly benefit the people. Details are provided separately below.

Inventory Quantity Surveys for Various Industries

In order to crack down on the hoarding of daily necessities and implement fair prices for daily necessities, Shanghai's trade associations have decided to handle matters in accordance with the "Measures for Cracking Down on Hoarding of Daily Necessities" and the "Measures for Fair Price Purchase and Sale of Daily Necessities" promulgated by the Ministry of Economic Affairs. They have already advised merchants to sell at fair prices and are conducting inventory quantity surveys for various industries. Those who refuse to be surveyed, deliberately provide false survey data, refuse to sell daily necessities at fair prices, or deliberately raise the prices of goods in an attempt to profit will be dealt with in accordance with Article 14 of the "Emergency Period Price Fixing and Anti-Speculation Measures." The so-called daily necessities refer only to those necessary for people's clothing, food, and use.

Four Banks to Pay for Fair Price Purchase and Sale

Regarding stabilizing commodity prices, a fair price purchase and sale office can be established. The operating funds of the purchase and sale office will be allocated in installments by the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Farmers Bank of China according to actual needs. However, its accounting will be directly audited and supervised by the four banks. If the profits of the purchase and sale office are insufficient to cover expenses, resulting in a loss of operating funds, the government may allocate funds to supplement it. However, the profit margin is stipulated not to exceed 5% of the cost. In the Shanghai Concession area, in addition to rice already being sold at a fair price, flour being sold at a fair price, and coal balls being sold at a fair price, it is hoped that all industries dealing in other daily necessities will uniformly promote fair prices.

Aimed at Curbing Illegal Trade

The English-language "Da Mei Evening News" reported that the French Concession's Board of Directors had declared "war" on those who hoard and speculate for profit and on the rising cost of living. The French Consulate has just issued a new order authorizing the Board of Directors to set maximum prices for daily necessities. According to French Consul General and Chairman of the Board of Directors, Eugène, he told reporters that they felt obliged to take this measure for the public interest and not merely for the interests of the Board of Directors. They were not trying to hinder legitimate business, but to curb illegal trade. In addition, the French Concession decided not to increase taxes, so as not to provide any stimulus to rising prices.

Merchants' Inventory to be Investigated

The new order stipulates the following: The goods stored by merchants will be fully investigated, and those who violate the order will have their goods confiscated and distributed or sold publicly to the poor. A committee will be organized to investigate all details of commercial transactions, determine the original price and current selling price of various foods and other items, identify instances of excessive pricing, and investigate transportation costs, etc., and then determine the permissible profit margin. The committee will ask merchants to allow the committee to inspect their accounts and check their inventory, as the new order has granted full authority to the committee.

Legitimate Profits Will Still Be Maintained

The committee will proceed with a firm approach in setting price limits. For example, for goods whose original price and transportation costs have not increased significantly due to the war, the maximum price will be set according to the average prices of 1935, 1936, and 1937. For goods whose original price has indeed risen, the maximum price will be set according to the original price plus a reasonable profit. For goods whose original price is not easily estimated, the maximum price will be set according to its capital plus a reasonable profit. An increase of a certain percentage in various commodity prices will be allowed to compensate for labor or additional expenses.

Government-Set Prices for Surplus Goods

The committee will study the causes of price fluctuations, and if necessary, may ask the Consulate General to take charge or authorize a department of the Board of Directors to handle the sale of any kind of goods. If the committee deems it appropriate, it may ask the Consulate General to require merchants to sell surplus inventory at government-set prices to meet urgent needs. Those who buy or sell goods in quantities greater than all existing goods, or who engage in futures trading (such as paying the difference in price without delivering the goods), will be fined from one yuan to one thousand yuan.

Public Concession Considers Measures

The same penalties will be imposed for selling at prices higher than the limit, concealing inventory and falsely reporting sales on the black market, refusing to show documents, or refusing to allow inspection of inventory. The French Board of Directors has not consulted the Shanghai Municipal Council on this new plan. However, according to Municipal Council Secretary-General, Phillips, the Public Concession authorities are not ignoring this general issue and will have to consider a plan of a similar nature. For example, the Municipal Council's cooperation with flour mills to sell flour at fair prices is one of the Municipal Council's actions to alleviate the people's suffering.

Since the Japanese Navy Special Landing Forces announced the cancellation of "passes" and the full opening of bridges along the Suzhou Creek and the two gaps on North Jiangxi Road on the 16th of this month, in an attempt to entice citizens to return and restore the market in the occupied area, the barbed wire on North Jiangxi Road, from the Delin Apartment side to Bazi Road, has been completely moved to the center of the road. However, after the opening, feeling that the pedestrians entering and exiting were mixed, they have strengthened security, paying special attention to those who tidy up the bridges.

Arbitrary Arrests of Residents and Pedestrians

The Japanese side recently received a secret report that a leader of the Central Special Agents secretly brought 30 to 40 staff members to Shanghai, and secretly sent personnel into Hongkou to take action. They have become unusually paranoid and panicked, subjecting newly entering residents and pedestrians to strict searches. Anyone suspected of being involved will be arbitrarily detained and tortured. According to people coming from Hongkou, the Japanese recently suddenly and forcibly conscripted able-bodied men in the Hongkou district, and about a thousand people have been arrested in recent days, all of whom have been taken to a certain Japanese warship and transferred to a certain place. As a result, the Chinese people are deeply wary and afraid to enter. There are very few pedestrians on the roads of Hongkou. Therefore, those returning to their old residences are still moving to the concessions to reside.

Five Java Ships Carrying Huge Amounts of Foreign Rice: Sailing Directly to Shanghai from Saigon and Rangoon; The First Ship Can Arrive on Sunday; Some Rice Shops Fined for Exceeding Price Limits 63

Since the national rice was blocked by a certain party and the source was obstructed, the price of rice has continued to rise, and the livelihood of the common people has been threatened. Although foreign rice has been arriving continuously, the price has also risen opportunistically, making it difficult for the common people to maintain their lives. Fortunately, the second fair-price sale has benefited the common people a lot. It is learned that in addition to the constant and large-scale transshipment of foreign rice from Hong Kong, a large batch is also being directly transported from Saigon and Rangoon. The Shanghai Tanhua Postal Ship Company has specially dispatched the "Tjibesar," the "Sawah Roonto," and the "Slogen" to Saigon and Rangoon to transport foreign rice. The first ship, "Tjibesar," is expected to arrive in Shanghai this Sunday (the 25th). The amount it is carrying is currently unknown, but the exact number will not be known until the ship arrives in Shanghai, and the number must be huge. With such a large amount of rice being transported, the price of foreign rice in the city is expected to fall.

Rice Merchants Punished

In order to strictly enforce price limits and prevent hoarding and monopoly in order to suppress rice prices, the Public Concession's Municipal Council has recently severely punished rice merchants who exceed the price limit. In the past two days, there have been many cases of people being detained and sentenced by the court for selling white rice at a price exceeding the limit. The day before yesterday, the Public Concession's Political Department learned that the Taishan Rice Shop at No. 68 Henan Road was selling white rice at a price of more than 50 yuan per shi, so it ordered its staff to buy some, and it was indeed the case. Therefore, Hua Tan No. 361 went to arrest the shop's accountant, Li Shugen from Qingpu, and the shop assistant, Gu Mingde from Jiading. It was found that none of the rice sold in the shop's accounts was below 50 yuan. Yesterday morning, Li and Gu were sent to the Ninth Criminal Division of the Special First Court for prosecution according to law. After questioning by Judge Sheng Shengxiu, Li Shugen and Gu Mingde were sentenced to 15 days of detention each as a warning.

Fair-Price Sale Begins

After the Shanghai Fair-Price Sale Committee decided to entrust the Rice Shops Association to handle the second phase of the fair-price sale, the Rice Shops Association has designated 48 members in the Public Concession and 32 members in the French Concession to handle it, with a total of 40 fair-price sale locations. Each location will be issued a white cloth signboard by the Fair-Price Sale Committee, with the words "Shanghai Fair-Price Sale Committee, No. 〇 Location" and the words "Rice Distribution" or "Ticket Sale." Due to the patrol officers maintaining order, the fair-price sale time has been changed to 1:30 PM to 6:30 PM every day. Each location will distribute 50 bags of broken rice per day until it is sold out. One French currency can buy five and a half catties of rice, which is equivalent to three and a half sheng (approximately five catties and ten taels). At the entrance of the fair-price sale location, there is a notice from the Concession authorities' police, advising rice buyers to be mindful of good deeds, strictly abide by order, and not cause trouble. Those who are unruly and cause trouble at the rice shops will be immediately arrested and severely punished. The second phase of the fair-price sale is scheduled to begin today.

Japanese Will Use Large Sums of Money to Connect with American Missionaries in China: The Act of Buying Goodwill with Money is Base; American Missionaries Have Unanimously Refused to Accept and Have Sent a Large Number of Christians to China to Engage in Activities 64

"The Mainland Evening News" reported yesterday (the 21st) that according to responsible persons of the American Church in the city, Japanese political figures have suggested providing financial assistance to American missionaries in China in an attempt to buy American sympathy favorable to Japan. As for the news from Tokyo that the Japanese government has allocated 10 million Japanese yen to subsidize Japanese friendship organizations and connect with the American Church, there is nothing to be surprised about.

Japanese Christians Come to China to Engage in Activities

This Japanese attempt aims to influence the attitude of the Chinese people in the occupied areas towards Caucasians, so that American missionaries will write to their friends in the United States, reporting on the activities of the Japanese in China that are favorable to Japan. The above suggestion is now under consideration in the Japanese Diet. However, some Japanese Christians have been selected and sent to China to engage in activities. Their main narrative will be to cultivate the goodwill of American missionaries in China.

Suggest Allocating 10 Million Yuan

It is understood that the news of the above suggestion was first released in Tokyo last Sunday, including a suggestion from a member of the Seiyukai Reformist faction to allocate 10 million yuan for the above task. Japanese Foreign Minister Arita stated in the Diet that he would consider and study the suggestion in detail. However, according to a missionary, "The Japanese cannot buy goodwill with money. The people's hatred of the Japanese is deeply rooted. If we accept any kind of assistance, we will be suspected of colluding with the enemy."

Using Means to Obscure Everything

Members of the American Church unanimously believe that the Japanese suggestion is aimed at indirectly affecting American sympathy towards Japan. According to a missionary, many well-informed Japanese believe that the letters sent by missionaries to friends in the General Assembly and other organizations have a great influence on the policies adopted by the American government. The Japanese are now trying to cover up the evil deeds they have committed, which have been revealed in these letters, and only intend to use means to obscure the eyes of the missionaries, hoping that the missionaries will praise the Japanese in their future letters.

Hosting Banquets and Making Overtures to Connect

Regarding the Japanese attempt to win the friendship of American missionaries, a missionary recalled that the Japanese often held banquets or other gatherings in the occupied areas, inviting missionaries to participate. However, when American missionaries receive invitations, they often consult with their Chinese colleagues to ensure that accepting the invitation will not be seen as being subservient to the Japanese.

Banks and Pawnshops Refuse Gold Collateral: All Gold Held as Collateral Must be Registered and Reported 65

The Ministry of Finance previously approved the decision of the National Defense Supreme Council to strengthen the government's wartime gold reserves. In late autumn of last year, it explicitly prohibited banks, pawnshops, silver shops across the country from storing, pawning, and exchanging gold, and designated the Chongqing Central Bank of China's head office to be responsible for handling the exchange of gold for legal tender. It is now learned from separate letters to the Shanghai Banking and Finance Association that, regardless of gold that has already been pawned or is prepared to be pawned, the Shanghai branch of the Central Bank of China should be informed in detail at any time to serve as a basis for exchanging legal tender, etc. It is heard that after receiving the letter, the two industries have separately ordered their affiliated banks and pawnshops to comply. According to a spokesperson for the financial community speaking to a reporter from Datong News Agency, in addition to complying with the ministry's order to prohibit banks and pawnshops from storing gold collateral, the banking and finance industry has also complied with the Central Bank's letter to register and report the gold already held as collateral to the Shanghai branch of the Central Bank in detail. The reason why banks and pawnshops have recently refused to accept gold collateral is to comply with the ministry's instructions. Secondly, the gold collateral business is less stable than commodity collateral, because the price of gold may rise or fall sharply at any time. Banks and pawnshops cannot profit from rising prices, and will inevitably suffer losses if pawners redeem their collateral upon maturity when prices fall, because the pawners will not redeem the pawned goods.

Coal Briquette Factory Should Maximize Production During Price Control Period; Traditionally, Production Exceeds Sales; Strictly Prevent Inferior Materials in Controlled Price Coal Briquettes 66

Coal and Firewood Dealers Please Provide Spot Goods to Aid the Poor

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent two letters to the Shanghai Machine-Made Coal Briquette Trade Association yesterday, stating: (1) Respectfully addressing, regarding the matter of coal briquette price control, it should be complemented by each coal briquette factory maximizing production to regulate supply and demand. This matter has already been resolved by your council, and our chamber has sent a special letter to your association, requesting that you distribute it to the relevant businesses to comply with the record. However, regarding the actual production situation, whether it can achieve the maximum extent should be investigated by your association sending personnel to the factories every day, creating a report of their daily output, factory by factory, for assessment and comparison, so that the original intention of the resolution can be thoroughly implemented. It is hoped that you will investigate and handle this matter. Furthermore, according to the industry's key figures, the traditional production volume of the coal briquette industry is around 1,500 tons per day, while the sales volume is only over 1,000 tons. If each factory can continue to maximize production as usual, there is no need to worry about shortages. We are also providing this information. (2) Respectfully addressing, regarding the holders of coal briquette warehouse receipts, your association has previously resolved, and our chamber has jointly announced, that they should pay the warehouse rent and release the briquettes within ten days, from February 20th to the 29th. Sales should be stopped after the deadline. Your association is requested to investigate and report the name of the holder, the quantity of briquettes in storage, the warehouse receipt number, and the original price at that time, one by one, and list them in a report, as a basis for handling the matter according to the resolution. This is a matter of great importance. It is reported that the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce also sent letters to the Public Concession’s Municipal Council and the French Concession’s Board of Directors yesterday, requesting that they instruct the police authorities to take care of the various coal briquette shops selling at controlled prices in order to protect them. However, according to letters from various residents within the concession, the coal briquettes purchased in recent days contain a lot of mud and little coal, indicating a reduction in materials. This may be the work of a small number of coal briquette merchants, and the industry should step up efforts to expose them.

Small-Scale Coal Briquettes to Be Delivered Separately

The Shanghai Machine-Made Coal Briquette Trade Association held a joint meeting of representatives from various factories at 10:00 AM yesterday. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent Yan Esheng to provide guidance. Chairman Chen Cuifang first reported the purpose of the meeting, and each representative reported the situation of selling coal briquettes at controlled prices. Immediately afterwards, resolutions were discussed and passed: (1) A letter requesting Hancheng, Tongcheng, Damao, and Three Companies to open up coal dust cases was resolved and passed. A copy of the letter is recorded. (2) Small-scale deliveries requiring store delivery will add 20 cents for delivery, and the Chamber of Commerce will issue a notice to alleviate the suffering of overcrowding. The resolution was passed. (3) The movement to reduce water transport costs was resolved and passed. (4) The price control issue will be discussed and resolved by each public group in a proper manner. (5) The factory production volume will be reported to the Chamber of Commerce for record-keeping. The resolution was passed. The meeting adjourned at around 1:00 PM.

Order Issued to Prohibit Price Gouging

The Shanghai Firewood and Charcoal Trade Association received a letter from Wu Shaoshu, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, yesterday, instructing them to urge member firewood and charcoal shops to strictly abide by the joint announcement of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Coal Briquette Charity Association, to implement the sale of coal briquettes at controlled prices. Those who do not comply with the stipulated prices, arbitrarily raise prices, or claim to be out of stock and refuse to sell will be severely punished. At the same time, those who hoard coal briquettes for profit will be thoroughly investigated and dealt with.

Coal and Firewood Dealers Please Provide Spot Goods

The Shanghai Coal Merchants United Association sent a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and other parties yesterday, stating: Respectfully, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Machine-Made Coal Briquette Trade Association jointly issued a notice of relief coal briquettes this month on the 20th, suppressing the selling price of coal briquettes to stabilize the market. We express our sincere sympathy. Our association has recently received reports from various member merchants stating that the goods released by various coal briquette factories are entirely for the needs of warehouse receipt holders to pick up goods. There are occasional small amounts of coal briquettes supplied, and even some county brands have stopped wholesale. As a result, it is impossible to wholesale spot goods without warehouse receipts.

Shops Will Have No Goods for Sale

Or a few have some stock, and it is difficult to maintain several days of business. Customers are unaware and believe that the firewood and charcoal shops are using the excuse of being out of stock to refuse to sell at controlled prices, resulting in many disputes. A remedy needs to be discussed. It is requested that the factories supply each firewood and charcoal shop with the daily amount of spot coal briquettes sold to maintain business. The letter also stated that the members of our association are all small-scale coal and firewood shops, and coal briquettes are one of their side businesses. In recent years, the prices of various fuels have increased, and it has become even worse recently. Although the price of coal briquettes has also increased,

In Terms of Effectiveness,

it is more economical than other fuels and has become a necessity for fuel users. The firewood and charcoal shops have also shifted from a side business to a large-scale sales item. Most of the firewood and charcoal shops are operated with small capital, and recently, all purchases require cash transactions. Door sales are sold as soon as they are wholesaled in order to turn over capital. Those with slightly thicker capital can only prepare a few days' worth of sales. They rely on upstream suppliers to supply spot goods at any time to meet the market. The retail price is also based on changes in the purchase price in order to maintain costs and slightly reduce expenses. The customers are the general poor households who make up the largest number of city residents. Their purchases range from two or three cents

To Less Than One Yuan.

This is because their economic strength is weak and their housing is cramped, so they cannot buy in large quantities. The above is the situation of the small-scale coal and firewood shop business, which is significantly different from large-scale capital operations. Now, the coal briquettes from each factory are entirely for the needs of warehouse receipt holders to pick up goods. Firewood and charcoal shops without warehouse receipts will inevitably run out of stock and have nothing to sell. Each factory's coal briquettes are sold at controlled prices, and each person is limited to one load. Poor households have no ability to buy in loads. The firewood and charcoal shops are also out of stock. In this situation, there is a real risk of running out of food. The method of each factory selling coal briquettes at controlled prices is very good. However, the attention is not yet paid to this group of people with the lowest purchasing power.

Poor Households

have not been paid attention to, and it seems that the relief is not comprehensive. I believe that since the factory is willing to fulfill its responsibility for relief, it should not ignore the fuel for these poor households. If each factory can supply each firewood and charcoal shop with the daily amount of spot coal briquettes sold at controlled prices, and each firewood and charcoal shop also sells them at controlled prices in the market, and if there are any unexpected price increases, please have the authorities sanction them. If this is the case, then the general poor can all buy coal briquettes at controlled prices, and each firewood and charcoal shop can continue its business. This is the most appropriate way to supplement the relief. I hope that your association will look into the above situation and adopt it, and please ask each coal briquette factory to supply goods immediately to maintain business and stabilize the market. We are grateful for your cooperation.

White Russian Youth Invents Truck Load Measuring Device; Experts Tested It Yesterday Morning and Found It Very Accurate; Still Needs Improvement and Plans to Sell to American Automakers 68

The English-language "Shanghai Evening Post and Mercury" reported that the city's thoroughfares and bridges are easily damaged by trucks with excessive loads. The police department finds the procedures complicated and difficult to prove that trucks are overloaded, which makes it difficult to arrest them. This has become a traffic problem. Now, a White Russian youth named G. Timoloyov, who has lived in Shanghai for eleven years, has invented a truck load measuring device. The device costs very little to manufacture but is very applicable. The measuring device is shaped like a box and is installed between the truck's spring and the body. A wired battery connects to a special indicator installed near the front windshield of the truck. At a glance, you can tell whether the truck is overloaded. This (22nd) morning, Mr. Gan invited technical experts from the Public Concession Police Department and the Health Department to view the measuring device's test. A truck was used to carry 8,500 pounds of goods, which was then increased to 9,000 pounds. The weight shown by the measuring device was indeed accurate. Afterwards, Mr. Gan stated that he plans to wait another half a year to improve the device and then hopes to sell it to American automakers.

Police Department Solicits Residents to Install Alarm Systems

During this extraordinary period, thieves are rampant, and Shanghai residents often feel disturbed. In view of this, the Public Concession's Municipal Council's police authorities are planning a prevention plan and soliciting public support. If each household installs a simple and effective alarm, not only can the whole family be kept safe forever, but it can also assist the police authorities in eliminating crime and stabilizing society. If any household intends to install one, they can go to the nearest police station to obtain a brochure on the alarm system. If you want to test it in person, you can visit Room 303, 3rd Floor, Public Concession Police Department, No. 185 Fuzhou Road, during daily office hours to contact them.
