Finance Many Foreign Exchange Longs Turn to Selling 77

Yesterday's foreign exchange market saw HSBC's listed rates unchanged. The gray market for British and American exchange rates started tight but loosened, ultimately stabilizing, mainly due to the influx of telegraphic transfers from Hong Kong. Initially, overseas rates for US and British exchange rose by one cent, leading to an opening market showing a stable British rate and a looser American rate. Subsequently, due to forceful buying by Chinese banks such as Shanghai and speculators and foreign firms, the market briefly tightened and weakened. At 9:45 AM, British gold reached 4/1/5625, and the US exchange rate reached 6.84375 yuan. Later, due to the sudden influx of telegraphic transfers from Hong Kong, some profit-taking by Sassoon's long positions, and some sales by those holding floating long positions for the current month, the market stabilized. After 11:00 AM, there was little discussion or trading, and the market was quiet. In the early afternoon, continued selling by Chinese merchants holding positions for the current month and further sales of telegraphic transfers from Hong Kong caused rates to briefly rise to 4/2/03125 and 6.9375 yuan, respectively. Finally, Chinese merchants returned to buy forward contracts, so at the close, British gold was still 4/1/875, and the US exchange rate was still 6.90625 yuan. As a result, British exchange was stable, and American exchange rose by 0.03125 compared to the previous day. The swap rate for this month and March was about 1.09375 US cents for banks, equivalent to a monthly interest rate of 1.6375%, or about 1.38% per month.

Yesterday's cash gold bar gray market continued its meandering trend, generally fluctuating around 48 yuan. As a result, it continued to fall by 18 yuan. However, as the foreign exchange market turned from tight to stable, market sentiment frequently shifted. Securities Foreign Stocks Still High; Domestic Debt Sold Off in Large Quantities; Impartial Observer Offers Impartial Commentary 81

Since this newspaper successively disclosed the manuscripts of Mr. Xin Wei Jian Ying and Mr. Xin An, it has aroused the interest of readers in the industry. Yesterday, a letter was received from Mr. Chi Ping, whose words were quite reasonable. Therefore, the original letter will be disclosed, and readers will wonder what their thoughts are. The original letter from Mr. Chi Ping reads:

"The organization of a modern nation, to sum up its outline, consists of people, administration, land, and currency. Among the four, currency is the major artery. There has never been a nation that could stand and last with an unsound currency. Our country, since the outbreak of the War of Resistance, has long planned for the overall currency situation, so in the first year or two, it always stood within the legal price. This is enough to prove that the legal tender has a great power that cannot be shaken, and there is no doubt about it. Later, the war shifted westward, the ports were closed, and customs authority was destroyed. 'Joint Notes' and 'Hua Xing' were successively established, and those who plotted against us used currency to exchange currency and arbitrage foreign exchange, thus launching the initial stage of the bilateral economic war. The decline in the value of the currency against foreign currencies was a necessary measure. People, unaware of the decline in the value of the currency, became frightened and competed to hoard goods, buy gold, purchase drafts, and hide foreign stocks and real estate to escape the calculation of funds. They do not know that this kind of foolish action is both laughable and pitiful. Looking at the gold pound and the US dollar, before the war, every five US dollars could be exchanged for one gold pound. Now it is four dollars and two cents in London and three dollars and eighty-nine cents in New York, a considerable difference. However, this difference is not because the United Kingdom is unable to maintain it, but because maintaining it would benefit international investors. Therefore, for the sake of the United States, it is necessary to proceed cautiously. Our country's current currency policy has the same intention, and it is not that it is unable to maintain it at seven or eight pence or one shilling, because it is afraid of the Japanese's clever plundering, which would prolong their economic collapse. All Chinese people should recognize this point and engage in mass production to enrich national power during the European war. This is the only way. Now, before the end of the lunar year, speculators in Shanghai are hoarding goods, gold, foreign stocks, and drafts in large quantities, fearing that they will not be able to make a profit. They are creating groundless rumors to make the second batch of wealthy merchants continue to follow suit, causing the prices of everything to soar and people to panic, as if a great disaster is about to come. They do not know that the first batch of big speculators have already slowly withdrawn, making a great profit, while those who follow suit are still dreaming. Taking foreign stocks as an example, except for Kai Ping, Electricity, Tramway, Waterworks, and International Trust, which are on track and can be invested in, the most unconscious are Public Utility stocks, Rubber stocks, and Shipbuilding stocks. Public Utility stocks have a contract relationship with the Municipal Council and do not have generous interest. There is no reason for them to exceed the face value by more than one cent, so exceeding the face value by two or three times is unreasonable. The rise and fall of the company's assets should be calculated for silver company stocks, and the face value should not be forgotten and interest should be used for conversion. The value of shipbuilding stocks should be calculated according to the profit standard of the previous year. If it rises to four times, even if there is profit, it is self-inflicted. When settling accounts for rubber stocks, they are also calculated according to the face value in Chinese currency and not calculated according to the current value and market price because of exchange rate changes. The cheapest cost per pound is more than 13 cents (due to increased wages and income tax), and the most expensive is more than 25 cents. The current market price is the best, which is 38 cents as reported in the daily telegram, and the second best is only worth about 30 cents, and there is a fixed limit on shipments, which are sold by a general company. If the average sales proceeds of last year are calculated with the current market price, small rubber stocks can yield 2% interest, medium rubber stocks can yield 4% interest, and large rubber stocks can yield 6% or 7% interest. Only two months remain this year, and there is a very long time to go. The changes in the situation are just beginning. If Willkie's trip to Europe is successful, then peace is in sight, and it is not impossible for the price of rubber to fall to 30 cents upon entry. The Japanese are actively advancing south, and the defense of the Far East is weak. If they are occupied, the danger at that time should also be considered. Looking at the market prices of six months ago and the current market prices, I know that those who are slightly clear about the economic situation must be surprised and sigh at how rare this is. In short, compared to the financial situation of the last European war, it was as high as nine shillings during the war and immediately dropped to about two shillings after the war. Once the war in the Far East ends, the legal price can undoubtedly be established immediately. If you want to exchange back the currency at that time, I know that the difference will be considerable. The wealthy merchants and those who follow suit now have to consider this carefully."

Yesterday's stock market at the Chamber of Commerce was very bullish again. Jardine Matheson, Union Wharf, and Steelworks shares saw new highs, and trading volume was huge. Although there was profit-taking, the selling pressure was not significant. Jardine Spinning shares rose to 39.5 yuan, and rubber shares remained strong.

Stock transactions: 200 shares of China International Trust Company were traded at 9.5 yuan, and another 200 shares were traded at 96 yuan, up more than 30 cents from before.

London, 21st—Today, the listed prices of Chinese foreign debt remained stable, and there were no changes in the bonds across the board.

Because Deutfraco sold enthusiastically, about 700,000 to 800,000 shares, the market price suddenly felt unsustainable and fell sharply without any recovery. It was rumored that it was due to the expiration of bank loan periods and the calling in of goods, which shows that the economic situation is not as significant as political changes. Trading therefore suddenly increased, and funds therefore suddenly loosened. This kind of decline entirely belonged to the relationship between supply and demand and was not of great importance. However, as Deutfraco's selling pressure became increasingly strong, even with the buying of Jiu Feng Lian He Tai Feng, the supply still exceeded demand besides Deutfraco's continuous sales, and Tian Sheng Shun Li Da Tong Yong Feng successively sold off. Commentary

No Need to Follow 95

— Fu Yong

According to various sources, gambling dens in the Shanghai West Extra-Settlement Road area have received notices to close by the end of this month. This is the first step in the formal implementation of the "Western District Agreement." While it may not be "overwhelmingly popular," at least the Shanghai West area, which has been "bad" for nearly two years, will no longer see "paradise" or "entertainment venue"-style scams.

Of course, the "special individuals" who "make a living from this" will definitely not give up. Under their diligent "activities" and "maneuvering," the Nanshi area will succeed Shanghai West as the "second bad place." All harmful, sinister dens are busily preparing and arranging to take advantage of an even more powerful backing to "grandly open for business" once again.

If it doesn't come from the west, it comes from the south. It's the same old thing for the gambling den bosses. But what about the patrons who "pay tribute" with the price of their hard-earned money? Are they also thinking of gambling in the south if they can't gamble in the west, and creating more moving and tragic stories for the social news pages?

We don't need to bring up many stories of embezzlement or suicide by hanging, because every patron's motto is "everyone knows how to gamble, but each has different skills." They believe they won't end up like those people, driven to desperation. However, "relocating" requires fees, "protection" requires salaries, car service costs money, fruit and cigarettes aren't free, and the ultimate "backer" requires huge commissions. Under such enormous expenses, "skill" is already someone else's magic weapon.

Don't gamble! No need to follow!

Can't Buy Coal Briquettes, Let Alone "Fair Price" Coal Briquettes 96

— A certain person

Since the price of coal briquettes rose to seven yuan per dan, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Machine-Made Coal Briquette Trade Association specially entrusted 18 coal briquette factories, including Yitaixing, to sell at a fair price. Although the selling price was still 5.80 yuan per dan, it was still an exciting piece of news.

However, this fair-price sale method does not reduce the suffering of citizens, but instead adds many troubles. Most families of the salaried class buy one dan to burn one dan, and they all get it from nearby coal shops. This time, the fair-price sale was limited to 18 coal briquette factories, and coal shops did not receive any of the fair-price coal briquettes, so all the large and small coal shops were unable to supply the market. Even if they had inventory, most of them could not sell at the fair price of 5.80 yuan due to cost considerations, cutting off their customers. The 18 coal briquette factories, although stipulated to be open from 7:00 AM to 7:00 PM, most of them were already out of stock by noon.

Therefore, in addition to "group coal purchases" and "strict punishment of hoarding" being promptly implemented and strictly enforced, during this period of transition, the method of selling coal briquettes at a fair price should be improved. Otherwise, the Coal Briquette Trade Association will not only waste its efforts, but will also appear to be deliberately using "fair-price sales" as a means of gaining fame and reputation.

We believe that in addition to the 18 coal briquette factories, perhaps due to procedural issues, not every coal shop can be assigned fair-price goods. At least, based on the concentration of residences, divide them into several districts, and assign several fair-price coal briquettes to several coal shops in each district, because with the daily demand for coal briquettes in the city, 18 coal briquette factories will definitely not be able to cope. Secondly, increase the quantity as much as possible, and secretly send people to investigate whether each factory is underreporting its production or whether there are still hidden deals to raise prices.

In short, like selling flour at a fair price, dealing with things superficially is of no help in practice, but instead creates more malpractices. Please everyone put in a little effort to do things, and also please everyone have a conscience when doing business.

After the Rain, the Sky Clears 97

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 21: Blending Economics with Fiber, Using Machinery to Aid Writing

Let's talk about Ye Jinfen's father, who came up with this idea to help Jiang Jingrong. Originally, the Ye family were from Hangzhou, and they were a capitalist class. They opened a silk shop in Hangzhou, and later opened another silk shop in Shanghai. In the past, silk fabrics in China were mainly produced in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and among Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, the silk fabrics produced in Suzhou in Jiangsu province and Hangzhou in Zhejiang province were the most famous and valuable. Those silk satin and gauze have always been woven with wooden looms. The patterns are indeed being updated, but the weaving methods are still the same old ones. They never opened any factories, but simply distributed the raw materials to each weaving household, who took them home to weave and then sent them back. These weaving households were often distributed inside and outside the cities of Suzhou and Hangzhou. However, as world transportation became increasingly frequent, all foreign products gradually sold in China. Silk fabrics were also like this. Products from England, France, Germany, Italy, and even Japan and India were all dumped in China. Because China has a large population and a large market, and Chinese people like novelty and showing off, they rush to buy those imported goods, which are bright in color and novel in pattern. This human love of novelty and curiosity cannot be stopped, unless you don't allow them to be imported, but that can't be done either. However, China's inherent silk fabrics have been greatly affected by it. The ancient sage said that when you are poor, you change; when you change, you get through. This is an unchanging principle. So you have to improve your inherent silk fabrics. You must cater to current tastes and no longer stick to old methods. Therefore, wooden looms are gradually being changed to iron looms; what used to be distributed to each weaving household is now concentrated in one place; those who never set up factories in the past are now setting up factories. Ye Songfen's father was an improver of silk fabrics. He first set up a silk weaving factory in Hangzhou, improved many silk fabrics, and achieved great results. Later, he set up another silk weaving factory in Shanghai, and is currently expanding it, wanting to set up a branch factory, so he had to train some talents in the textile industry. Ye Songfen is like Jiang Jingrong, he is an only son, but Jiang Jingrong has two younger sisters, while he has two older sisters. His eldest sister is already married, and his second sister is still studying at a girls' school. And like Jiang Jingrong, he is also thirteen years old this year, but Jiang Jingrong's birthday is in the first half of the year, while his is in the second half of the year. The next day, Ye Songfen discussed his father's idea with Jiang Jingrong. Jiang Jingrong said, "Then don't I have to live in your factory? Originally, when I came back from selling newspapers, I could still help Mom do things, and I could also teach my younger sisters to read. Wouldn't this all be unsuccessful?" (241)

The Problem of Elementary School Students Eating Snacks 98

— Xin Liang

Every elementary school student, I can say here very definitely and certainly, there is not one who does not like to eat snacks. The money they ask their parents for is probably used to buy things like coffee candy, bubble gum, chicken cakes, heart-piercing biscuits, etc. And no matter what time, whether it is a good time to go to school in the morning, a good time to finish lunch at noon, or a good time to get out of school in the evening, as long as they have money with them, as long as their mouths are empty, they are happy to crowd into the "vending department" attached to the school, or go to those sugar stalls outside the school gate to buy food to eat.

The result of eating snacks, needless to say, is of course not beneficial at all. First, it is wasteful, and third, eating snacks can also cause children to develop a kind of gastrointestinal disease. Children often have stomachaches, and most of the reason is probably because they eat too many snacks.

For the sake of saving money, for the sake of protecting the studies and health of our children, I think the problem of elementary school students eating snacks is indeed worth discussing here.

My personal opinion is that in order to prohibit elementary school students from eating snacks, the school authorities and parents should bear joint responsibility. Below are a few scattered articles. Dear readers, please feel free to discuss them.

(1) On the school side:

A: The "vending department" can only sell books and other school supplies, and absolutely not sell snacks such as candy and biscuits.

B: Students who bring snacks to school to eat should be punished by the school, such as being fined for copying books, writing characters, etc.

C: Teachers should often tell students about the harms of eating snacks.

(2) On the parents' side:

A: As parents, you absolutely should not give money to your children to eat snacks. You must know that this kind of giving money cannot be considered love. Protecting your children's studies and health is even more important.

B: As parents, you should prepare a piggy bank or "saving box" to cultivate a habit of thrift in your children.

Managers and Junior Staff 99

— Simon

According to reports: The deputy manager of ×× company, usually looks down on junior staff, is very arrogant, and often loses his temper. As a result, the staff in his department have very bad relations with him. When they could no longer bear it, they jointly sent a letter to the board of directors, listing six major offenses. But it aroused the manager's dissatisfaction, who considered it an insult and hired a lawyer to sue in court.

Let's put aside for the moment the question of who is right and who is wrong in this matter, and how the court will rule. But in fact, managers, with a few exceptions, are often arrogant, bad-tempered, and look down on junior staff, scolding them when they want to. People who have been junior staff have probably all tasted this flavor, right? In fact, managers do less work every day than junior staff and get paid more. Junior staff, on the other hand, work non-stop all day long and get only a small amount of salary. Their year-round labor is for the manager's benefit. If there were no junior staff, the manager probably wouldn't be able to do all the work, and their high salary would have nowhere to come from.

As the saying goes: No matter how good the peony is, it needs the support of the leaves. Although managers have extraordinary talent, without junior staff to serve him and do his work, I'm afraid no business can develop. There is indeed a distinction between managers and junior staff in terms of position, but in terms of occupation, managers and junior staff have the same contribution to social undertakings.

Therefore, for any business to succeed, managers should understand that junior staff also have a share of the credit, and it is not something they have achieved single-handedly. If they understand this point, then not only should they not look down on junior staff, but they should also sympathize with them for their heavy workload and meager salaries, and often provide comfort in spirit, and never put on airs as managers. If they can do this, even if junior staff have a difficult life, they will no longer discriminate against the manager, and their work efficiency will increase instead.

Movie Stars in Shadow City are Eager to Learn 101

— Hua Zhi

Hollywood movie stars who aspire to advance are studying hard while filming, and are very self-disciplined.

For example, Jimmy Cagney, he was originally a medical school student and wanted to be a doctor, but because his family was poor, he dropped out of school and went into movies. He is currently saving money to continue his studies.

Miss Olivia de Havilland, she graduated from a music school with honors. Although she is good at performing tragedies on the screen, she continues to study music and is preparing to become a professional pianist soon.

Spencer Tracy, who won the Academy Award for Film Arts last year, studied at Marquette University and hoped to become a lawyer after graduation. As a result, he entered the film industry due to economic pressure. Now he is still studying law on his own.

Betty Davis, the master of tragedy, was originally a top student at Garrison Professional School, specializing in history. Once, because her romance with a male classmate broke down, she angrily entered the screen. Now she feels that life is very monotonous and is also reviewing ancient books.

There are also the beautiful Priscilla Lane and her two sisters. They are all college students and take a study abroad approach. Before entering Hollywood, they traveled around with dance troupes and audited courses at various universities when they had time, regretting that they could not complete a full degree program. Now she is also tutoring in her spare time.

The luckiest one can be said to be child star Shirley Temple, who is still of school age. Fox Company hired many teachers to teach her. Among the teachers, there are those who are knowledgeable and those who are knowledgeable about current affairs, artists, and writers, all kinds of people. I'm just afraid she doesn't have time to study. Compared to others who dropped out of school, she is truly a darling of heaven.

Pinocchio Goes to the Bottom of the Sea to Find His Father 103

Movie Story

The Adventures of Pinocchio 104

— Translated by Ivan

Searching for His Father at the Bottom of the Sea

Pinocchio Goes to the Bottom of the Sea to Find His Father

In the midst of the wind and clouds, they flew all night long. When the sun returned to the earth, they came to a cliff. The sea roared below, and the surging waves were like a busy giant. Here they said goodbye to the pigeons. Pinocchio tied a piece of yellow stone to the donkey's tail, and he and Jiminy jumped down and sank straight to the bottom of the sea. The sea kingdom is really a wonderful place, with all kinds of fish and all kinds of seaweed and coral. But Pinocchio was determined to find his father and had no intention of looking at this spectacle. He bumped east, asked west, and searched the bottom of the sea, but he couldn't find the sea monster whale. He shouted loudly, "Father! Father!" But the only answer was his own echo.

Not far from here, a deserted island was floating on the surface of the sea. This is the sea monster who is dozing off. In the depths of his throat lives a poor old man, the pitiful old Geppetto. He and the kitten Figaro and the goldfish Cleo have been without food for several days. They all hope that the whale king will wake up and swallow some fish so that they can continue their dark days for a few more days. Pinocchio's loud shouts woke up the sea monster, who opened his mouth wide and sucked a Sally-like wooden idol into his mouth. But he left the cricket still floating on the sea. (9)

Anecdotes from the Pear Garden 105

— Xu Muyun

The Amusing Story of a Certain Prince Performing a Show to Raise Money (Part 2)

It happened to be the end of the year and the creditors were pressing on the prince's door. The prince could only sigh and block them out. A certain righteous actor heard about this and said to his colleagues, "The prince used to spend money and see money, and he was very close to our Pear Garden line. He didn't put on any princely airs at all. Moreover, no matter what kind of performance was held in the prince's mansion, (he always spoke well for us in front of his family. Therefore, we earned a lot of money from him (the prince often served as the director of the show), so we can't ignore him in this difficult situation. Why don't we all put on a show to raise money and invite the prince to join in the performance? On the surface, we're helping others, but in reality, all the money we earn will go to him." Everyone agreed when they heard this. That day, the theater was full. Logically, after deducting the expenses for the front stage and the band, there could be a surplus of several hundred yuan, which could be used to tide over the New Year comfortably. Who knew that although the prince was poor, his style when he went out was still about the same as before. Moreover, he had good relationships with people, and people in the backstage had always received benefits from him. When he stepped into the backstage, he was still dressed neatly, with a servant carrying his white flag costume bag behind him, without any sign of poverty. So, bowing and greeting were still as warm as before. After the prince finished his performance, the backstage crew was busy taking off his makeup, taking off his boots, and serving him attentively. Of course, it was the same as before, and the words of hard work and compliments were even more lively than before. He was so happy in his heart that he committed the extravagant habit of a young master again and forgot all about his family's poverty. So he distributed all the money he had earned as rewards. The supporting actors got thirty or fifty yuan, and the box managers and servants got ten or eight yuan. In a short while, all the money was used up. When he came out of the backstage, he saw a group of creditors coming up to him. These people came with great hope, but they didn't expect to get a single penny. The prince could only cough and sigh as he walked, and the creditors followed dejectedly. The show to raise money that they had pinned their hopes on was sung in vain. (185)

"A Sky Full of Stars" Completed Filming 106

— Nan Lin

"China Electric" Location Shooting Team Leaves Kunming for Chongqing

(Kunming Airline News) The "China Electric" location shooting team of thirty-eight people, led by the business section chief Li Gongge, left Chongqing for Kunming in October last year and immediately began shooting location scenes. Apart from a few days when the work was suspended due to illness, they were working hard every day. The main task of the team in Kunming this time was to shoot location scenes for "A Sky Full of Stars," followed by the "China Electric" troupe's public performance. This was the first time the troupe had performed in Kunming. On December 12 last year, the troupe gave its first public performance of the four-act play "Frontier Storm," written by Yang Hansheng and directed by Shen Xida, at the People's Education Center on Wenmiao Street. It was performed every night at 7:30 PM for several days, and the box office was quite successful. Then they performed "Demons Run Wild," written by Chen Baichen and directed by Sun Yu. The performance of this play was very good, full of tragicomic humor and satire, and was very popular with the audience. The troupe also donated all the proceeds from one day's ticket sales, after deducting expenses, to the Air Defense Command to cover air defense expenses.

In addition to shooting location scenes for "A Sky Full of Stars" and performing plays, the team also filmed a newsreel of the Yunnan Army's expedition on the spot. The content was quite magnificent. The team stayed in Kunming for three and a half months, and all the personnel left Kunming for Chongqing on July 30. The location shooting for "A Sky Full of Stars" was also completed.

Wu Mei at Meilongzhen 107

— Hua

The Shanghai Drama Society is going to revive "Women's Apartment." Wu Mei plays the landlady of the women's apartment in "Women's Apartment," and she is successful. In later performances of "Women's Apartment," she always played the landlady. When Yihua Company adapted "Women's Apartment" into a movie, director Chen Yunran also asked someone to ask her to play the landlady as a guest star, but she was busy with other things at the time and did not agree. But the nickname of landlady has been added to her head, and it is "old brand."

Recently, she and a few friends have jointly opened the Meilongzhen Restaurant on Weihai Road. She personally goes to the Xiaocai Market on Sima Road at 5:00 in the morning every day to buy food, and she takes care of the affairs in the store in the afternoon. When friends from the drama troupe come to the town for a short stay, she always asks for their opinions on snacks and dishes, just like she asks for criticism when she is acting.

Wu Mei is really practicing being a landlady, but she still hasn't forgotten the drama she loves. Now she is busy rehearsing "Guilian" every night. The Drama Society's revival of "Women's Apartment" may also take time to play the landlady again.
